## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential growth to density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance model)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (quadratic density-dependent growth)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects including Allee)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth rate)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (changing environment over time)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with saturating reproduction minus mortality)
- Weak Allee with logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P / (1 + c3 * P)) (weak Allee effect via mate-finding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent mortality/competition â†’ quadratic term -c*P^2 appearing alongside linear growth c*P
- Allee effects (cooperative behavior at low density) â†’ cubic polynomial in P with sign changes, or multiplicative factor (P - c_threshold)
- Carrying capacity structure â†’ factor of form (1 - P/K) multiplying growth term, creating a zero-crossing at equilibrium
- Metabolic scaling in growth â†’ fractional powers of P (e.g., P^(2/3) vs P) reflecting surface-to-volume relationships
- Seasonal or periodic environmental forcing â†’ multiplicative sinusoidal modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) on growth parameters
- Multiple equilibria in population â†’ polynomial in P with multiple real roots indicating stable/unstable fixed points
- Saturating per-capita growth rate â†’ rational function forms like c*P/(1+c*P) replacing linear terms
- Logarithmic growth regulation â†’ log(P) terms indicating Gompertz-type multiplicative degradation of growth rate
- Time-dependent environmental degradation â†’ exponential or linear functions of t multiplying carrying capacity terms
- Conservation of growth symmetry â†’ if dP_dt is symmetric about a midpoint population, suggests logistic-family models
